Educational News

Ministry of Education Stipulates Principles for Normal School Students' Service

Students are not allowed to further their education or engage in professions outside the education sector during the prescribed service period.

Affiliated Elementary Schools and Kindergartens Should be Established for Practice

The Ministry of Education, considering that the operations of normal schools in various provinces, cities, and counties nationwide are generally inadequate, that affiliated elementary schools and kindergartens have not been fully established, and that graduates have not been adequately placed or assigned by the educational administrative agencies of the respective provinces, cities, and counties, has specially formulated the "Regulations on Service Principles for Normal School Graduates" and the "Rules and Measures for the Establishment of Affiliated Elementary Schools and Kindergartens by Normal Schools." These will be circulated to the educational administrative agencies of various provinces and cities in the coming days for their information. The two sets of regulations are hereby recorded below:

Service Regulations

(1) The service period for normal school graduates shall be calculated by doubling their study period. (2) Each graduating class of normal schools shall be assigned by the educational administrative agencies of the respective provinces, cities, and counties to various localities to serve as teachers in elementary schools or equivalent institutions. (3) Graduates of normal schools and special normal courses may serve as elementary school teachers, and graduates of kindergarten courses may serve as kindergarten and junior elementary school teachers. (4) Normal school graduates shall not be allowed to further their education or engage in professions outside the education sector during the prescribed service period. Violators shall be required to refund their tuition and board fees, and if they have entered a school for further studies, the school shall be ordered to expel them. However, under special circumstances, with the approval of the provincial or municipal education administrative agency, their service period may be extended.

Affiliated Elementary Schools

(1) Normal schools should establish affiliated elementary schools and may also establish affiliated kindergartens to facilitate students' practice and experimentation in elementary education. (2) The affiliated elementary school shall have a principal, appointed by the normal school principal from qualified personnel, and reported to the competent education administrative agency for record. (3) The affiliated elementary school and kindergarten should be located near the normal school. (4) The affiliated elementary school should lead the study and experimentation of elementary education issues in nearby counties to seek improvements.

League of Nations Initiates Film Teaching in Schools of All Levels in Various Countries

Entrusts China with the Organization of Educational Groups

The International Educational Film Association of the League of Nations, in order to promote the development of educational films as supplementary teaching tools, plans to organize film teaching groups composed of outstanding teachers from schools of all levels in various countries who are willing to dedicate their time and effort to film teaching, naming them "Educational Film Pioneers." A brief plan has been formulated and entrusted to the China Educational Film Association to organize the Chinese film teaching group. The China Educational Film Association believes that film teaching has attracted the attention of educators in China in recent years. It plans to send letters to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to inquire about teachers' opinions on film teaching in various schools in order to organize this group and seek cooperation. The original letter from the League of Nations is translated below:

Letter from the International Educational Film Association to the China Educational Film Association, Dear Sir, Our association has been working hard to promote the development of educational films as supplementary teaching tools. The representatives of various countries at the last International Conference on Educational Films unanimously approved. We feel that the activities of our association in this direction need to be disseminated to ensure the direct and organized cooperation of the best representatives of the entire teaching world.

We believe that the success of adopting teaching films as teaching tools and how to make organized use of them is closely related to the attitude of teachers in general towards this issue. Therefore, our association decided to launch a joint solicitation of "groups in various countries that use films as supplementary teaching tools," and in the future, a national organization will be established at the association's location. Teachers in general, whether in words or actions, who express their willingness to spend time and effort to make beneficial efforts on teaching films, deeply know that students can get great results from this wonderful auxiliary tool.

This group, named "Educational Film Pioneers," the Rome Association is convinced that teachers can give considerable support and, as a result, a group that can use the energy of young people can demand and get the entire use of films in schools around the world.

Educational Film Pioneers are teachers, and at the same time, the most suitable cooperator and consultant for publicizing to colleagues and school authorities, so that they can finally prepare tools for schools in their respective countries to use films in schools. The Rome Headquarters will prepare a simple, clear and applicable plan, the implementation of which depends on groups in various countries using films as supplementary teaching tools. This plan will be the basis for various regulations. The regulations are the same for groups in various countries. The main points of this plan are as follows: A. Promote the use of teaching films by teachers through special lectures and organize psychological, technical, and teaching training. B. Promote the establishment of a technical and psychological committee, trusted by the school authorities, to entrust the production of teaching films and supervise their full use. C. The committee must coordinate teaching films with school curricula and textbooks. To the extent possible, the government should stipulate the subjects of various courses. In various schools, it should be made as suitable as possible for the presentation of films.

D. Directly organize, or jointly organize with school authorities, various competitions for school teachers and technical experts. According to the technical and psychological committee, the subject matter of educational films of various subjects is proposed.

E. Raise funds, and it is necessary to ensure that at least one set of film projection equipment must be available in schools of any level, whether in rural or urban areas, which can be used for school lessons.

F. Strive to promote the organization and establishment of school film libraries, and at the same time take into account their recurring expenses.

The above are the main points, and other detailed methods will be added at any time to improve them.

We sincerely hope that people from all countries who are enthusiastic about supporting this initiative will cooperate with our association to make this pioneering career for the benefit of students around the world a success.

We respectfully entrust your association to organize this group in your country to promote the use of teaching films in your country, so that we can achieve our common mission. I hope that you can be an important partner of our association and look forward to good news. President De Fiero,

Ministry of Education Favors

Students from Border Provinces

Revising the Regulations on the Treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan Students

The Same Treatment for the Provinces of Xinjiang, Gansu, Kang, and Ningxia

In recent years, the number of students from border areas coming to Beijing to study has gradually increased. The Ministry of Education has formulated regulations on the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students to facilitate their admission. In order to broaden the scope, it is proposed that students from Xinjiang, Gansu, Xikang, and Ningxia provinces should also be entitled to the same treatment. The regulations have been revised and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. The revised regulations are excerpted below:

Revised Regulations on the Treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan Students, Article 1, Mongolian and Tibetan students coming to the Central Government and various provinces for study shall be treated in accordance with these Regulations, unless otherwise specified. Article 2, The following agencies may recommend Mongolian and Tibetan students to the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission or its Beijing Office before the start of the school term each year, but must provide the student's: (1) name, (2) gender, (3) age, (4) place of origin, (5) academic qualifications, (6) character evaluation, (7) language skills, and attach two 2.5-inch photos of the student. (1) Mongolian league and banner official offices, (2) Tibetan local official offices, (3) Mongolian and Tibetan schools at all levels, (4) Provincial and county governments along the border connected with Mongolia and Tibet. Article 3, The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission or its Beijing Office should clearly transfer the students recommended by various agencies to schools at all levels. If there are vacancies in the schools, they should accept these students. Except for those who meet the qualifications and can be placed in the appropriate class, all are regarded as auditors, but only those who can directly listen to lectures. Whether they are formal or auditors, all schools that admit Mongolian and Tibetan students should report to the Ministry of Education separately or forward them for record. Article 4, Mongolian and Tibetan auditors who pass the academic year examination in each school should be changed to formal students of this class, and those who fail are still auditors. A certificate of attendance is given after the auditing period expires. Article 5, Each school should send the academic year results or graduation results of Mongolian and Tibetan students to the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission at the end of each academic year for separate awards or recommendations to equivalent schools at home and abroad for further studies. Article 6, Mongolian and Tibetan students who graduate from specialized or higher education institutions may be selected by the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission for recommendation, and various agencies may distribute them to serve in Mongolian and Tibetan areas. Article 7, Mongolian and Tibetan students who are introduced by the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission or its Beijing Office should be exempted from all tuition fees in public schools and should be given appropriate reductions in private schools. Article 8, If there are regulations such as subsidies and sending students to study abroad for general formal students in various schools, formal Mongolian and Tibetan students should receive the same treatment. Article 9, The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and its Beijing Office shall provide appropriate hospitality to Mongolian and Tibetan students who come to Beijing and Ping for the first time to study and who are proven to be true. Article 10, If any Mongolian and Tibetan students in various schools are found to be imposters, in addition to expelling the student, all expenses incurred by the student shall be recovered from the original sending agency or its guarantor. Article 11, Students from Xinjiang and Xikang provinces who come to the Central Government and various provinces for study may be treated in accordance with these Regulations. The recommending agencies are the provincial and county governments and schools at all levels where the students are located. Article 12, Students from Qinghai and Ningxia provinces who come to the Central Government and various provinces for study may be treated in accordance with Articles 3, 4, and 7 of these Regulations. The recommending agencies shall be handled in accordance with Article 11. Article 13, Students from Gansu Province who come to the Central Government and various provinces for study with qualified graduation certificates shall be treated in accordance with Articles 3 and 4 of these Regulations. The recommending agencies shall be as stipulated in Article 11. Article 14, If there are any matters not covered in these Regulations, the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education may submit them to the Executive Yuan for transfer to the National Government for approval and revision. Article 15, These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center

Proceeding with Editing Daily Newspaper Indexes

Decided to Include Various Daily Newspapers in Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, and Other Places

This Kind of Undertaking Is Still an Original Creation in the Country

Daily newspaper indexes are only seen in large-scale newspaper offices in various countries. Other cultural institutions rarely hold them. The Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center, in view of the fact that daily newspapers are a ledger of the activities of the entire society, and a measure of the transfer of personnel, which become historical materials after time passes, will inevitably have many omissions without an index. However, the classification is cumbersome, the procedures are complicated, and it is several times more than magazine indexes. Now, after a long period of research by the center, the classification items have been properly drafted and started. The newspapers on which it is based are decided to be major daily newspapers in Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, Guangzhou, Wuhan, and other cities. The method is different from newspaper clippings, but the function is roughly the same. This kind of undertaking is still an original creation in the country.

China Arts and Crafts Society

Publishing Consulting Work is Tense

Authors Come to Register

The China Arts and Crafts Society, in view of the increasing complexity of social affairs and personnel, and in order to meet the needs of young people, planned to set up a personnel consulting office this spring. The Re-launched Issue of Educational Magazine is Published

Educational Magazine was founded by the Commercial Press in the late Qing Dynasty and has been published continuously for more than 20 years. It is a major authority among educational publications in China. Its contribution to the improvement of education in China has long been recognized by educators. However, the "January 28th" Incident occurred in 1932, and the general factory of the Commercial Press was destroyed, and Educational Magazine was also suspended. When the museum resumed business, due to the limitation of production capacity, only the four major magazines, such as the East, were relaunched first. In recent years, the printing work of the museum has made great progress, and all aspects of our country are striving for the revival movement. The voice of education to save the country is particularly high. The re-launch of Educational Magazine cannot be delayed. The museum has been preparing for several months, and the re-launched issue of Educational Magazine was finally re-launched on the 10th of this month to meet with the Chinese people. The magazine is edited by He Bingsong and has more than 70 special writers, all of whom are educational experts in the country. The authors who wrote for the inaugural issue, in addition to the staff of the society, include Wang Shijie, Wang Yunwu, Feng Zikai, Chang Daozhi, Zhang Qixian, Jiang Wenyu, Zhao Yan, Cheng Qibao, Ma Zongrong, Chen Lijiang, Du Zuozhou, Jiang Qi, Zhuang Zexuan, Gao Juefu, Shen Yougan, He Qingru, Zhong Daozan, Yu Ziyi, Zhao Tingwei, Zhou Xianwen, etc., more than 30 people, each expressing their grand opinions, which is a grand view. It is also heard that the magazine is now offering a half-price pre-order method, 12 issues for the whole year, only receiving 90 cents, as a commemoration of the re-launch.

Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

Contribution Talk

This Week

— Yang Yan

There are some good news in the Chinese goods industry this week:

The education authorities have issued a notice that all student uniform supplies must be purchased from domestic goods. Chairman Chiang of Nanchang has issued a notice that all formal dresses nationwide must be made of domestic goods.

The Minister of Industry is paying attention to the overseas promotion of domestic goods and has ordered the International Trade Bureau to actively carry out the promotion.

The Women's National Goods Year Movement Committee is holding mobile exhibitions in various schools and sending personnel to various places to promote the use of domestic goods.

The China National Goods Company, in conjunction with nine major domestic goods factories, held a temporary national goods market to commemorate the "September 18th" Incident.

The Family Industry Society has initiated a joint exhibition of domestic cosmetics by various factories in the same industry.

From the above news, we feel that the life and future of Chinese domestic goods are very promising. The administrative authorities are sincerely helping, the social figures are enthusiastically proceeding, and the domestic goods companies and domestic goods factories themselves are also seizing the opportunity to constantly exert their strength to contribute to society. What is especially worth commemorating is the China National Goods Company's temporary national goods market commemorating the "September 18th" Incident. It brings together the achievements of nine factories to commemorate publicly, with far-reaching implications and profound significance. Some people said angrily: "One commemoration, two commemorations, three commemorations, all are fantasies. We have been living in fantasies for three years, and the lessons learned have been enough. The only way out is to repay eye for eye, tooth for tooth, cannon against cannon, bomber against bomber. We believe that armed self-defense can maintain national survival." This statement is very reasonable, but I would like to add one more sentence: "Our only way out is to be self-sufficient in every paper and needle, not to rely on foreign countries for every cup and basin, not to let foreigners and enemies earn my money in any way. We believe that economic self-defense can maintain the permanent survival of the nation." Therefore, to commemorate this painful "September 18th" Incident, we should never forget to use domestic goods at all times, and we should contribute to society at all times, so that we will not fail to live up to this meaningful commemoration.

But there is a bad contradictory news, which is that Guangdong Province levies special taxes on goods from other provinces, which contains the meaning of feudal separatism and is tantamount to destroying the domestic goods of the country. I think if you really love the country and have a conscience, you will always hope that this news is not true.

"National hatred has not been avenged and our hearts are still hot. Why should we rely on others for our needs?" Chinese people with ambition and blood, wake up!

Discussion of National Goods

The Crisis and Salvation of the Future of National Products

— Xuan Wan

The future of the domestic product production industry, fraught with difficulties and lurking dangers, seems to be dominated by fate, filled with "many disasters and hardships," constantly facing the onslaught of storms without any chance of relaxation. This year, American inflation has raised silver prices, attempting to achieve industrial prosperity through exchange rate manipulation and the large-scale dumping of goods at a loss in various parts of our country. This alone is enough to stifle our nascent domestic products. Recently, the newly promulgated customs tariffs, with their reduction of various import taxes, have dealt an even more forceful blow. Surrounded by an atmosphere of overproduction, "shutdowns," and "work reductions," those engaged in domestic products are deeply disheartened. However, "adversity strengthens the nation," the best encouragement from the ancients, "the darker it is, the more eager the heart seeks light." We should embrace this spirit to overcome current suffering and expand future paths.

When discussing policies to rescue domestic products from their current predicament, there are many, but broadly speaking, they all boil down to two shortcuts: encouraging all Chinese people to use domestic products and expanding international trade. It would be even better if both could be pursued simultaneously. I dare to briefly discuss them as follows:

1. Deeply Rooted in the People: "Promoting domestic products" must strive for depth and universality among the people. Empty slogans shouted by a portion of the city are useless, as everyone knows. Therefore, the wave of domestic product exhibitions in various places in recent years is a preliminary effort to publicize and introduce these products. The greatness of the recent Northwest Exhibition and the importance of the missions of the Huazhong and Huabei inspection teams organized by various factories occupy a significant position in the process of domestic products reaching the interior. What we particularly hope for is that domestic product companies in various regions can be established on schedule, forming a national network of domestic products. The recent opening of the Zhengzhou domestic product company and the preparations in Wenzhou and Jiaxing, which are reportedly nearing completion and will be officially inaugurated soon, will undoubtedly add a unique luster to the future of our domestic products.

2. Expanding Overseas: China is inherently a vast country with abundant resources. However, due to our own immature technology and backward production, we are instead subjected to the invasion of goods from industrially advanced countries. In fact, if we can vigorously improve various products and strive for perfection, why wouldn't we have a large number of exportable goods? Recently, it was reported that the International Trade Bureau, considering that our country's products have historically been handled by foreign firms, has specially introduced British and American merchants for direct procurement. Furthermore, an American merchant is actively preparing to collect over 150 kinds of domestic products and will ship them to Europe and America for promotion on a regular basis. This is indeed a great blessing for the future of our domestic products. In various parts of Southeast Asia, due to the strong patriotism of overseas Chinese, now is the time to boycott foreign goods, and it is imperative to promote our domestic products in these areas, a golden opportunity that should not be missed.

Do not be discouraged, do not be disheartened. "Only struggle is the way out." We should embrace this spirit to defeat evil and find light.

The Basic Work of Promoting Domestic Products

— Bian Beichen

In the minds of nine out of ten uneducated Chinese, they may not know what patriotism is, but their vanity is particularly strong. Daily life, including clothing, food, housing, and transportation, relies entirely on European and American goods, which has led to the current economic panic and the recession of domestic industrial and commercial enterprises.

Therefore, inferior domestic manufacturers, in order to cater to the psychology of customers who love foreign goods, or in other words, for the sake of making money, use names similar to foreign goods on their products, or print many foreign words on the boxes and packaging of their products, even without a single Chinese character. In this way, they become Westernized! Westernization can enable cold-blooded animals who do not know foreign languages but prefer foreign goods to buy in large quantities.

Here, I must clarify that I am not fundamentally opposed to domestic manufacturers using foreign languages on their products if their products are sold abroad. However, their products are sold entirely within the country!

At the same time, I also feel that using foreign languages on one's own domestic products can mislead those who genuinely love domestic products but lack the ability to distinguish them.

I believe that to promote domestic products, it is necessary to implement basic work. What is the basic work? First, the Chinese people should abandon the mentality of worshiping foreign goods. Second, domestic products should not use foreign languages unless they are sold abroad. If this can be done consistently, it will definitely be successful in three years!

Discussions on Domestic Products

Small Customs Should Be Under Martial Law

— Zhang Zhang

The role of customs is twofold: to prevent the entry of foreign goods and to protect the country's production industry. Its impact on the overall national economy and people's livelihood is extremely significant. Therefore, any independent country, or a country that hopes to survive freely and equally in the world, has absolute autonomy over customs, because it is truly the lifeline of the national economy and people's livelihood.

However, in China, since the opening of maritime trade, the power of tariffs has been controlled by foreigners. Therefore, the so-called "customs" not only cannot fulfill the responsibility of protecting domestic industry and commerce, but also serves as a gateway for foreign goods to enter the country, resulting in a growing trade deficit year after year, and the national economy and people's livelihood are becoming increasingly strained. We find this situation extremely painful and hope that the government authorities will have autonomous control over tariffs, reduce the trade deficit, and alleviate the economic hardship of the people.

Accordingly, we can say that the major customs, which are related to the overall national economy and people's livelihood, should resolutely become autonomous. In other words, they should be placed under strict martial law to prevent foreign goods from crossing the line. However, at the same time, let us take a step back and think that strict martial law should also be imposed on the small customs on each individual. What is the meaning of martial law on individual small customs? This means that to prevent the invasion of foreign goods, on the national level, we should certainly use the power of the government to strive for full autonomy of tariffs. On the individual level, in addition to wearing and using various necessities, we should try our best to use domestic products. At the same time, we must not allow foreign goods to enter our food, which is my explanation of why small customs should be under martial law.

Don't you believe it? Please read the news published in various newspapers on September 1:

"International Trade Bureau news: The value of shark fins imported for entertaining guests by the upper and middle classes in the first seven months of this year was 8,980,072 gold units, equivalent to 1,791,653 yuan in national currency, a significant increase compared to the same period last year, when it was only 1,280,730 yuan, an increase of more than 500,000 yuan. In July alone, it was 1,085,555 gold units, equivalent to 216,567 yuan in national currency, most of which was consumed in this city. This shows the extravagance of the people in Shanghai," and so on.

Alas, upon seeing this news, the reporter could not help but sigh three times, believing that this is a disgrace to the Chinese people, especially the bourgeois class in Shanghai. In such a serious national crisis, everyone is still indulging in pleasure, which is a very infuriating matter.

Therefore, I am proposing the slogan that small customs should be under martial law and contributing it to the general bourgeois class and those who indulge in pleasure. Please pay attention to whether foreign goods are mixed into the imports of small customs from now on. In this way, the trade deficit may be reduced in the future, and the newspapers will no longer publish heartbreaking news.

This Publication's Announcement

The 86th issue of this publication, which should be published on September 20, will be published in advance on September 18 as a "Nine Factories' Domestic Products Temporary Special Issue" in commemoration. Contributions from readers should be around 300 words and have significant meaning.

From "Foreign Goods Stores" to "Domestic Products Companies"

— Ye Yiyi

Recently, domestic product companies have been established one after another, which we believe is a very good phenomenon. Domestic product companies collect domestic goods from all over the country, serving as a domestic product exhibition that allows local people to have a good understanding of domestic products. On the other hand, they gather the products of various domestic manufacturers, allowing inland people to have a good opportunity to choose and purchase them, which is an excellent method.

However, let us now examine the conflict between domestic and foreign goods in the inland areas, and the potential power of foreign goods in the inland areas.

We know that the organizations that promote both domestic and foreign goods are generally called "stores." The name "domestic product company" has only been heard in recent years! Then, before the name "domestic product company" existed, and even now that the name "domestic product company" exists, when people want to buy clothing materials, they always say, "Go to the foreign goods store!" This is the case in the inland areas, both in the past and now. Isn't it also the case in Shanghai? Friends, haven't you heard people say, "To buy clothing materials, go to the foreign goods stores in Xiaodongmen!"

In fact, the term "foreign goods store" has been deeply imprinted in the minds of the general public. Many people will always say "foreign goods store" without thinking. Even if a store sells domestic goods, or does not sell foreign goods at all, people will still call it "foreign goods store."

Alas! Thinking of this, how can we not be heartbroken? It seems that there are no domestic goods besides "foreign goods," and that only "foreign" is worthy, and that "foreign" is the only merchandise. The word "domestic" has disappeared and no longer exists in dictionaries. Without "domestic," how can there be "goods"? Alas!

I personally believe that before widely establishing domestic product companies in the inland areas, we should pay attention to:

(1) Completely overthrow the name "foreign goods store" so that people no longer have this term in their minds. To achieve this, in addition to the self-awareness of the general public, we should also think of a method to make it a matter of great shame if one does not purchase goods from a "domestic product company."

(2) "Foreign goods stores" in the inland areas should specialize in selling foreign goods. Shopkeepers should be aware and stop selling foreign goods, establishing the signboard of "××" or "×××" domestic product company.

(3) When promoting "domestic product companies" in the inland areas, there should also be an organized and powerful guiding group. In addition, local education authorities should also cooperate.

(4) Propaganda is an effective policy.

Whether the above four points are appropriate, please give me your guidance!

Page 16

Free Talk

Chewing Words

— Ling Mo

Even now, I still feel it is a pity that Turkey abolished the Arabic alphabet and adopted the Latin alphabet. The Arabic alphabet is simple to learn and write, has strict rules, and can adapt to changes in language. Adopting the Latin alphabet only increases cumbersomeness, and it is inconvenient to learn block letters when learning to read and cursive script when writing.

Except for Chinese characters, most of the syllabic alphabets in Asia are better than the European-style phonetic alphabets. Certainty and simplicity are the most obvious. The abolition or retention of the two should at least have equal opportunities.

Language unity is a superficial rather than profound saying. The so-called unity means that the written text is read out as speech. As for how to write it and based on what to write it, there is a complex interaction of visual and auditory senses in the process. The complexity is an exchange rather than unity.

European-style writing sees an object visually, transforms it into auditory language, analyzes it into words audibly, transforms it into visual form, and then transforms it into language. Asian-style alphabets save one step of auditory analysis.

Theoretically, the process of constructing Chinese characters is even shorter. It goes from a visual object to a visual character and then to auditory language. Naturally, someone will say that a visual object must constitute an image of the object, and the image is the language. The process is not shorter. I don't want to argue about this statement. Our problem can avoid such complexity and be replaced by a simple mechanical statement.

Astronomers uniformly use ⊙ to represent the sun, and mathematicians uniformly use 　 to represent a triangle. If the visual object is not converted into sound by human light sensation, but into sound by mechanical light sensation, then the same machine will certainly convert it into the same sound.

In both aspects, it proves that humans are quite similar machines. History has made me complex. In unnecessary aspects, we should seek to reduce a little complexity. If mechanical language can be successful, expressing a certain image with a certain sound can achieve basic language unity.

The sound generated by current mechanical light sensation is inevitably wave-like. We may not be able to create a machine that can sense the light of shapes such as ⊙　 and convert it into a sound close to human voice. The wax discs of gramophone records and the wavy patterns on the film of sound movies can be converted into human language, but whether these wavy patterns can be created by humans and whether there is considerable freedom in creating them are all problems.

Perhaps the ideal of creating a form-meaning text that is commonly understood by all mankind should be abandoned in the end. Then we should now admit that unified phonetics is the only reform that can be achieved in the near future. There should also be some ideals under this reform, and it is not that the Latin alphabet can satisfy everything.

If a letter I can emit a bottom sound under a light-sensing machine, and MI two mothers can emit a rice sound, then promoting the Latin alphabet can naturally have permanent convenience. It is still unknown whether Westerners can have this achievement, and even if they can, it seems that the period is far away. As for the wavy patterns on wax discs and film, although they are now so complicated that they cannot be used daily, it is not a distant hope to improve them to be simple enough to become a new type of alphabet.

Filmmakers have hoped for several years to be able to create sound film copies in different languages in the study, borrowing the benefits of being simpler and more accurate than re-recording. After its success, they will inevitably further hope to simplify the drawing of wavy patterns, which should not be impossible to succeed.

Or some people think that since the human brain can make more ingenious reactions than machines, why wait for mechanical proof? However, the so-called ingenious reaction comes from the accumulation of energy. The inconvenience of Chinese characters is because they require longer training and accumulate more energy. If the machine can react equally, it not only proves that the reaction process is simple, but also that the machine can replace a part of the energy that needs to be spent, wouldn't it be better?

The first-style Mandarin phonetic symbols have always been ridiculed by linguists as being too clumsy, but in fact, the clumsiness of Roman style is only a matter of degree. What can be achieved by today's ideals has already been able to go beyond some.

Don't be afraid that the ideal alphabet is far away. You must know that even if we immediately promote the Latin alphabet, it cannot be popularized in less than ten years. Thinking that it can save the emergency is unreliable.

If it is for an emergency, the existing light-sensitive sounding reading machine is also a way. Try taking the reactions of various Chinese characters and observing the resulting sounds. It is not difficult to convert that sound wave into language, just like receiving wireless telegrams. But I am afraid that the sound wave is more complicated than the word, but we might as well try.

But the problem comes again, even if this road can be connected, after that book is converted into sound waves and then into language, can it really make the illiterate listen? Our current big problem is not that there is no way to chew words, but that there are too many ways to chew words.

Raft

— TK

How I Write a Script (Continued)

— Written by Olisa, translated by Yi Xian

He fell in love with Martha.

○ ○ ○

A lonely old man fell in love with a young woman.

Probably, at some time, he had cured her scarlet fever. She was thirteen years old then. He fell in love with this child then.

He recited the following lines about himself:

"With a farewell smile, love may make my desolate ending a little brighter."

Then cried. Once, he cried so hard that his collar was soaked.

A lonely doctor with a collar soaked in tears.

He thought he was an interesting person.

Why is he a doctor? In an article, I once said that the issue of weapons in drama affects scriptwriting. In this script, I am preparing for a murder scene. I use a doctor to plan this murder. It is easier for doctors to commit murder. That way, there are no obstacles. Doctors have poison, and even if they don't, it is always easy to get poison. Therefore, I gave the profession of doctor to the murderer. I imagine that this doctor loves art and loves the stage, and he has a special view of life. He looks at life through the prism of art. He can imagine unusual actions.

Martha came home from work.

The husband wondered, "Why are you so late?" She always comes home at the same time, but he always asks her why she is so late. That is his character. He is thinking about eating, and he is waiting for dinner. He sees that the reason that makes him feel hungry emerges in his wife's image.

Martha prepared the dinner that her father had started.

They sat down to eat dinner.

We try to use everyday conversations in this drama. That kind of messy, incoherent conversation that keeps changing topics.

They were eating dinner.

Husband (to Martha) "Hey, did you cut your hair?"

Martha: "Oh! I cut it yesterday! Didn't you see it?"

Husband: "Doctor Gefinkel is really something."

Father: "Martha, be careful. Look, you've soiled the tablecloth. I keep saying he's crazy."

Martha: "I didn't cut it too small, did I?"

Father: "What does it matter anyway? He's a stage doctor."

Husband: "He was sitting by the road all night. How come we don't have any matches?"

Martha: "You're making fun of him! He's a very nice person. I just saw the matches."

Father: "Look, every time I eat the last dessert, I always feel like it's too much."

Doctor Gefinkel came in.

They asked him why he was sitting by the road all night. The husband lay down on the couch.

Husband: "I came home and saw our doctor sitting there. What does that mean? At first, I didn't even recognize him."

Martha: (to her husband) "I'll get you a pillow."

Father: "Give him one."

Husband: (continues his story about the doctor) "And another thing - it was raining. Thank you, Marsha." (Marsha's nickname - translator's note)

Father: "That's right, it rained yesterday."

Husband: "That's where I saw Doctor Gefinkel sitting...."

The theme of this drama: A socialist society must be a complete society. Doctor Gefinkel came up with the following opinion: If the system of the whole society becomes better, then every member of the society must also become better. In a socialist society, people should be more pure and more noble.

This is Gefinkel's idea. He knows that there is some kind of struggle going on in the world, and he knows that it is a violent struggle. It is not right to show mercy to the enemy. However, the doctor is thinking about a classless society. In his opinion, a preparation is necessary to realize such a society. A classless society is a society where the relationship between people must be complete. This should be told to people. According to Gefinkel, in a classless society, one must pay attention to people's character and their improvement.

What he saw was:

A good woman loves a bad man. Martha loves an egoist. A shallow character, a person with the nature of a propertied class. How can this work? Is this right? Isn't there something wrong here? If there is something wrong here, then it must be explained and corrected. How can this be corrected?

Husband: "We were waiting for you, Doctor. You can tell us what you were doing by the road, right?"

Doctor: "I was trying to solve a problem."

Husband: "A problem?"

Doctor: "Yes. If in a socialist society, a good woman loves a bad man, what should be done?"

Husband: "What do you mean by a bad man? Do you think the world is made up of good people and bad people?"

Doctor: "That's what I think."

Husband: "Society is divided into classes, but it is not divided according to character."

Doctor: "I know this too, but I am still thinking about a classless society."

Husband: "Bah! Classless society is still far away - they say it will be completed by the end of the Second Five-Year Plan."

Doctor: "It's not that far."

Husband: "So, you think there won't be character struggles in a classless society?"

Doctor: "Yes."

Husband: "Interesting!"

Doctor: "Very interesting. For example, I think in a classless society, they would kill egoists."

Husband: "Nonsense!"

Food

The Futures Flour and Wheat Market is Quiet and Stable

---The Market Situation is Fluctuating, and There are Not Many Transactions---

After the flour market opened this morning, the market for each month generally presented a stable appearance. With the quotations for foreign wheat, Chicago rebounded by about 2 or 3 jiao, and Canada rose by 1 to 3 jiao. Therefore, after the opening price, the market for each month had stabilized, about 1 fen better than the closing price on the previous day. However, at a time when the country is suffering from water and drought disasters, the destruction of rural areas is increasing day by day. As a result, the daily purchasing power is also decreasing. Therefore, although the weather is getting light rain, people's hearts seem more relaxed, but the market value is already low, so the entry and exit of the exchange market are rare. When the afternoon market opened, transactions became even more sluggish. Both the trading parties were watching each other. The mainland gang stopped due to rain, and the guest gang waited quietly because the departure was not smooth. Therefore, there was little fluctuation up and down. As a result, this month fell by 1 fen and 2.5 li, October and November fell by 1 fen and 2.5 li, December rose by 0.5 fen, and January and February fell by 1 fen.

After the wheat market opened this morning, the market for each month had stabilized. The quotations for foreign wheat have all rebounded by about 1, 2, and 3 jiao. Therefore, the opening price for each month had a profit, about 2 or 3 fen better than the previous day. However, with the light rain in the world, the buying interest inside and outside the industry stopped. Transactions in each month were lonely, and there were many empty bids. When the afternoon market opened, transactions were relatively active, but mainland bulls were coming out, so in the fluctuation, it was slightly weaker. As a result, this month was better by 1 fen, October was slightly lower by 1 fen, November and December were better by 1 fen, and January was better by 2 fen. The spot wheat market has slightly turned stable and profitable. Because customers are tightening, factories are dealing, high goods are shouting high by 5 fen, medium and sub-grades are flat, and 5,000 packages of Shandong Xuzhou wheat are opened at 3 yuan and 6 jiao half, and sub-grade 5 jiao and 6 fen. Bengbu wheat 3 yuan and 6 jiao, sub-grade 5 jiao and 6 fen. Yingzhou wheat 3 yuan and 6 jiao half, Yaowan wheat 3 yuan and 6 jiao. It is estimated that Fuxin handled it.

He Buys a Shoe (Part 2)

— Cao Ming

In an instant, the wooden leg was snatched away, and the copper coins in his hand became his weapon. Glimpses of his past bravery flashed before his eyes. Accustomed to fighting, he was as excited as an enraged cricket, poised and ready. He suddenly stood up and lunged forward, but lost his balance and fell.

A policeman, like a statue with a fixed pose, emerged from the crowd, pushing aside the onlookers who were craning their necks, sticking out their tongues, and muttering criticisms, and indifferently shouted:

"What's going on? Fighting?..." He dutifully dragged the still-fist-swinging soldier up, his eyes scanning the surroundings.

The shop owner immediately turned around, his hands hanging down properly, and put on a polite demeanor:

"Ah, Officer, we businessmen value fair trade. Shoes must be bought in pairs. If everyone only buys one, we won't even be able to pay our taxes. This gentleman here... Even if he's from the 19th Route Army, let alone the 29th, I'm afraid I have to say no..."

"..." The policeman, uninterested, took off his hat and played with it, yawned, then furrowed his brows and said loudly, "We'll sort it out at the station. Go!"

The soldier, with curious yet disdainful eyes, tightly closed his wide mouth, supported himself with the wooden leg, and stood up. He caught sight of the paper box and, with the posture of a cat catching a mouse, reached out and grabbed it.

"Go to the station? That's fine. I haven't met your station chief yet." The soldier gave a cold smile. "Have I broken the law? What law? I don't understand. I only have one leg. I gave the other one to my dear compatriots. Asking you to give me a shoe is too much, but why can't I even buy one myself?"

The policeman faithfully carried out his duties, gesturing with two fingers to guide the chubby shop owner in autumn velvet trousers and the one-legged soldier ahead. The three mismatched figures limped towards the Yonghan South Road and the Yonghan Branch Bureau, gradually fading into the dusk.

The onlookers dispersed, seemingly satisfied. Only two or three rickshaw pullers and some wandering children curiously and furtively followed the three characters who looked like performers in a slapstick play.

On the Road

— Lin Xi

On the road: No home, just a hotel; treading on...

Even a familiar blade of grass, there's no heart to recognize anymore.

× × ×

Thinking of the front of the house, also thinking of the front of the hotel; the front of the house has a fence, the front of the hotel has a donkey eating grass.

× × ×

The sun shines on the familiar hills, familiar roads: there I am thinking of home, and a donkey's hooves shatter the bells.

× × ×

In the morning there is dew, in the evening there is fog; but there is no hotel, and no home.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Heaven

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter One: A Ghost Carries a Cart of Distant Guests from Guanzhong; A Family with Only Four Walls; A Ferry Crossing Laments Qin People

Apart from Li Shilian, even the chauffeur knows a little about the story of the Zhou and Qin dynasties. Pondering it, everyone feels that although Qin Shi Huang was a tyrant, his courage was truly great, and so they unanimously praised him. As they spoke, the tires suddenly went flat. The chauffeur got out to pump them up, and everyone else got out to stretch their legs. Beside the road was a fortress, and an old man with a white beard leaned against the fortress gate, sitting on the ground. Secretary Chang walked up and said: Old man, what's this place called? The old man said: This is an empty stockade, there's no water to drink. As he spoke, he leaned on the wall and stood up tremulously. He was probably deaf, as his answer didn't match the question. Cheng Zhiqian, precisely because it was an empty fortress, wanted to go inside and take a look. So, he walked ahead, venturing into the fortress gate. The fortress had neat earthen walls, but the gate was just an earthen hole, without a single piece of wood left. Inside the fortress was a straight road, with houses on both sides. However, all the houses were empty, with only four walls. People had haphazardly enclosed some land between the walls to plant some grain. At the center of the fortress was a crossroads, and looking around, all four directions were a jumble of earthen walls. Not only was there no sign of anyone, but not even the sound of human voices could be heard. In the gaps of the low walls, there was a whole cluster of green grass, and two yellow-haired, long-eared rabbits scurried away at the sound of strangers' voices. Secretary Chang said: Without these two small creatures, it would be fine, but with these two small creatures, it feels even more desolate. Speaking of which, this is the ancient capital of Qin Shi Huang, we descendants are truly ashamed. As he spoke, he turned his head and looked around. Cheng Zhiqian said: It's still the same saying, heaven does it, what can we say? At this time, Li Shilian also felt a stirring inside, and asked: Secretary Chang, although there are no people living in this fortress, the land is still being cultivated, so the common people must still be nearby. Are there any district chiefs or fortress chiefs? Secretary Chang said: Probably? Li Shilian said: If there are fortress chiefs, then it's alright, even if the fortress is more desolate. Cheng Zhiqian said: What do you mean by that, Mr. Li? Can a fortress chief relieve the famine? Li Shilian said: No, you see, the entire village is deserted, how will the government collect taxes? With a fortress chief, that doesn't matter. Find the fortress chief, and hold him responsible, and the taxes will naturally be collected. Everyone was stunned to hear his invention! (18)

Rickshaw

— Yan Qiao

I say: "The rickshaw in inland China is the vanguard of material civilization. Wherever there are rickshaws, all the new constructions and new supplies of the city are gradually transported over."

However, in Japan, the birthplace of the rickshaw, it is gradually decreasing due to the extreme development of other means of transportation. According to people from Japan, the fare for rickshaws there is sometimes even more expensive than for automobiles.

In the Shanghai-Suzhou area, rickshaws are called "yellow bag cars," probably because their color is yellow. On the Jinpu Railway across the Yangtze River, the rickshaws at each station are all black, so they are called "foreign cars," which is an abbreviation of "Eastern foreign cars." I remember that Suzhou also used to call them "Eastern foreign cars" many years ago. The term "Eastern foreign car" has been found in Mr. Wang Renqiu's "Xiangqi Building Diary," which says, "Yuanqing sent an Eastern foreign car, it seems very bumpy, because it's a strange car, I dare not ride it." That year was the sixth year of the Guangxu reign (1880), and Mr. Wang was a superintendent of education in Chengdu. Mr. Wang was used to riding in mule carts and two-handed carts, so he thought rickshaws were strange cars, but what was so strange about them? It also shows that he had a bit of a skeptical attitude towards emerging things. This was a chronic ailment of the literati and officials at the time, so it's no wonder that Li Chunkui opposed the construction of railways. But later, when Mr. Wang, with his small braid, took Zhou Ma to the old capital to meet Yuan Xiangcheng, what were his thoughts on the proliferation of rickshaws? I wonder if he ever tried this strange car?

Those who sing the high tune of humanitarianism think that riding in a rickshaw is inhumane, but in places where other means of transportation are not yet available, one cannot but ride in a rickshaw. Moreover, in China, where the livelihood of coolies is extremely difficult today, rickshaws have also relieved the hunger and cold of many people. Therefore, the Nanjing municipal government specially raised the fares of public buses to allow rickshaws to gain more patrons. To be honest, aren't they supporting rickshaws?

Privately owned rickshaws are most exquisite and prestigious in Suzhou; they are most reserved in Shanghai, but there is a kind of northern style, with a white cloth canopy and brass ornaments, which has a unique style and is very different from the Suzhou cars with embroidered cushions and carbide lamps. Just from this point, there is also a distinction between fortitude and gentleness.

Tidbits

— (Xu Jie)

The earth is a speck in space, man is a speck in the earth, so tiny that one can ignore it, what do gains and losses, honor and disgrace, matter to the heart?

All things begin from a point: a spore can become a tree of great size; a sperm can grow into a wise person; electrons and atoms are the mothers of all things: a point is truly the ancestor of the universe!

Points are gathered to form lines, lines are gathered to form surfaces, surfaces are gathered to form bodies, objects also originate from a point.

Records of Imperial Incense

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

If we were to strictly investigate, the Sino-Japanese War of Jiawu years (1894-1895), which caused China to suffer a great defeat and led to the handing over of the entire Korea to Japan, that humiliation, Yuan Shikai could indeed be directly listed as one of the culprits. The truth is this: he was originally a person of extreme impatience, especially fond of showing off his authority. He wished he could execute all the dissatisfied people with a wave of his hand. Unfortunately, the court did not understand this personality of his. When an emergency occurred in Korea, both China and Japan showed a tense state of affairs, but the court still wanted to strive to eliminate the war; therefore, it sent Yuan Shikai to Korea to mediate, hoping that he would be a flexible diplomat, using some clever means to negotiate with the Japanese and temporarily resolve various difficult issues. This, of course, also included the implication that China had no intention of fighting for the time being. Unexpectedly, after Yuan Shikai arrived in Korea, he acted solely on emotion, greatly offending the Japanese side; just at that time, the Japanese were no different from a newly emerged tiger cub, eager to find an opportunity to test their own military strength. Thus, they immediately issued an ultimatum and formally declared war on China. Thus, the history of China's national humiliation also began at the same time! What's even more ridiculous is that although the outcome of this incident was so bad, Yuan Shikai himself became famous instead. (Translator's note: This passage may not be consistent with the facts.)

In addition to this matter, Yuan Shikai also had a proud masterpiece in his life, which can also be regarded as his work of fame. This matter was not of great importance to the entire China; but the relationship with the Manchu government was indeed not small. If someone were to put it on the stage, it would surely be a tragedy that could be sung, wept, sighed, and hated. To narrate this incident, it is necessary to first discuss Yuan Shikai's character in detail. (127)

Crab Trap

— Yu Mengwo

The night has fallen into a deep sleep, and a gentle breeze blows from the river, causing slight ripples on the clear, still surface. Tiny stars twinkle scattered, and the moon is still hiding in the clouds, not yet emerging. I wander alone on the riverbank: appreciating and pursuing the autumn night of nature.

From the distant rustling reeds, several clear flute sounds are sent out intermittently with the wind; the dim light on the fishing boat is reflected on the green waves, flickering like falling stars in the sky.

Everything on this riverbank is so beautiful and full of poetry!

— Moon

The crab trap, woven from bamboo, is like a Great Wall around the heart of the river: the crab catchers, using their wisdom, set down a trap-like crab trap, light up bright lanterns, and wait for their target—the crab—to come, to repay the price of their laborious management.

The stupid crabs, unaware of the treachery of mankind, mistake the path of light, leading them to their doom without realizing it, how pitiful!

But, aren't the people in society also like this?

The Dried-Up West Lake

— (He Haisheng)

Heaven is not giving any rain, and Hangzhou has already had a severe drought for three months, so there is a water shortage recently. The salinity of the tap water is too high, and cooking tea and rice has a salty taste, making it difficult to swallow.

The beautiful West Lake is also gradually drying up, with water only in the deep center, and the shallow areas are already full of exposed mud. If you go to the Crane Releasing Pavilion on Gushan, you can already see the bridge piers of the West Lake Exposition Bridge. As for the fragrant and delicate lotus flowers, without the nourishment of the lake water, they are bare and planted in the mud, swaying in the wind, showing a haggard color.

There are still boats in the lake, but only two or three. Those melon-peel skiffs are all gathered on the shore, and the boatmen and women are sighing, complaining that heaven is not giving rain and cutting off their livelihoods.

The West Lake is dried up, and there is an even greater lack of drinking water, so wealthy people are driving to Hupao to fetch water, like the Shan Yin Road, but what will happen when the spring water is exhausted and there is not a drop left?

Local Chronicles

The City Outside the County Seat of Shanghai

— Shanghai Press Agency

The establishment of Shanghai County began in the twenty-ninth year of the Yuan Dynasty under Emperor Shizu, while the construction of the county seat began in the thirty-second year of the Ming Dynasty under Emperor Shizong. However, before the construction of the county seat, there were already many ancient cities within Shanghai's borders. However, due to their age and the lack of surviving sites, people rarely pay attention to them.

According to old records and research, the oldest walled city within Shanghai's borders is considered to be Helü City. The Geography of the Book of Han notes: "Lou County has Nanwu City, built by Helü to defend against Yue." The Taiping Huanyu Ji and the Supplement to the Wujun Tujing both say: "Thirty li east of Yuan Song's city, there are also two cities facing each other across the river, built by Helü to defend against Yue." The Shaoxi Yunjian Zhi quotes the above two sayings as one of the famous sites of Yunjian. Regarding the location of the city site, the Daqing Yitong Zhi says: "Nanwu City is sixty-five li southeast of Shanghai County, also known as Helü City," and the Huangchao Tongzhi believes it is sixty-five li south of Huating County, while the Jiaqing Shanghai County Zhi directly points out that Helü City is in the twenty-seventh bao of Shanghai. Except for the location indicated by the Tongzhi, which is more difficult to believe, according to the Taiping Huanyu Ji, the city site should be in the Yangjing district of Pudong, or even in the territory of Nanhui County; according to the Daqing Yitong Zhi, it should be southeast of Zhoupu; according to the Jiaqing County Zhi, it should be in the current territory of Gaochang, Caojing, and Fahua districts. As for its exact location, it is of course not easy to determine because more than two thousand years have passed and records from the Han and Tang dynasties are extremely lacking. However, the Supplement to the Wujun Tujing believes that the city was originally built to defend the sea route, so the credibility of what the Taiping Huanyu Ji says is naturally slightly higher.

The Hudu Fortress, commonly known as Luzi City, is written as Yuan Song's City in the Taiping Huanyu Ji, and as Yuan Shan Song's City in the Wu Di Ji and the Supplement to the Wujun Tujing. The Shaoxi Yunjian Zhi states that "on the side of the Hudu River, there used to be two cities, east and west. The east city was more than 10,000 bu wide and had four gates. Today, it has moved into the river. The west city is extremely small and is located northwest of the east city." According to the Biography of Yu Tan in the Jin Shu, Tan was the Prefect of Wu during the Yonghe period of Emperor Cheng, and due to famine and war, he repaired the Hudu Fortress to defend against sea bandits. Also, in the winter of the fourth year of the Long'an period of Emperor An of Jin, the Wu Prefect Yuan Shansong built the Hudu Fortress to defend against Sun En. The following year, En advanced from Gouyan and captured Hudu, and Song was killed. From this, it can be seen that the construction of the city was even before the Jin Dynasty. Later, due to erosion by the river, it was slightly damaged by the Tang Dynasty. By the Song Dynasty, it was half-destroyed in the river. During the Shaoxi period, only the southwest corner of the east city remained. There were still traces to visit in the Yuan and Ming dynasties. In the early Qing Dynasty, it had long become a level shoal on both banks, and the old traces were completely submerged. However, the water of the two Luzi Rivers beside the fortress still flowed north into the Wusong River. Since Shanghai opened up concessions, foreigners have filled rivers and built roads, and even the two Luzi Rivers have become intermittent and remnant ditches. According to the current address, the location of the east and west cities should be east of Xiaoshadu Road in the western district of the public concession, within the area south of the Sun Temple in Zhabei.

In addition to repairing the Hudu Fortress, Yuan Shansong also built a small city seven chi high and three hundred bu in circumference thirty-five li east of Huating County. The Tongzhi calls it Yuan Gong City, and the Daqing Yitong Zhi calls it Zhuye City according to the old name of Yunjian Zhi. The meaning of the two words "Zhuye" is no longer known, and the locals call both the city and the Yuan Shansong Temple east of the city the Zhuye General Temple. Today, the temple remains, but the city does not. It is located near Shagang in the Minhang district of Shanghai County.

The above five cities were all built before Shanghai County was established. During the Ming Dynasty, three fortress cities were built to defend against the invasion of Japanese pirates. Today, the two fortresses of Nanhui and Chuansha are under the jurisdiction of Nanhui County and Chuansha County, respectively, while the Baoshan Fortress City in the Gaoqiao district has also been submerged in the sea and cannot be traced. In the early Qing Dynasty, the Minister of War, Su Yi, patrolled the coastal areas and requested in a memorial in the seventeenth year of the Shunzhi reign to build an earthen city on the north bank of the Donggou of the Huangpu River, called the Zhai City. Government offices and barracks were set up inside, and a considerable force was stationed there to guard against the invasion of pirates. Later, because there was no trouble on the sea frontier, the earthen city soon collapsed and was not rebuilt. The garrisoned soldiers were also completely dismissed. Today, only those familiar with local anecdotes know that there was once an earthen city in that place.

Acknowledgments: The famous Chongming painter Cheng Zhaoxiang is a student of the famous calligrapher and painter Su Renquan and the Suzhou painting community veteran Fan Shaoyun. He is good at landscapes, and his brushstrokes are vigorous and unrestrained. He is highly respected by the people of Chongming. I am grateful to him for giving me a recent work yesterday, and I hereby express my gratitude and introduce him.
