Objective Environment

— A Long

For any problem, I must first think of a concrete or abstract solution before I dare to talk about it or start working on it. This is my personality, that is, my lack of knowledge and adventurousness.

I have the same attitude towards the problem of the mass language, so the first opinion I published on the mass language was to "discuss a smaller problem, should we discuss it separately or merge it?" My meaning is; since the mass language has been promoted, (1) we should first think about the organization and production methods of the mass language, (2) how to sell it to the masses? Regarding these two propositions, the former advocates using one dialect as the standard, because the Beijing dialect is more common and easier to implement, so assuming the use of Beijing language, the latter, the current masses, are mostly illiterate, so we should start with universal education first. Since universal education cannot be expected from the government, only the general intellectuals - those who claim to be representatives - should automatically take the lead in doing this work. These are some of the opinions I contributed in the article "A Smaller Problem."

But recently, I have seen and received (mostly with abuse and talking about things outside the problem, the supplement of this newspaper generally does not publish) texts opposing me, mostly talking about empty theories without regard to facts, or even talking about things outside the problem. Therefore, I cannot help but be a little more presumptuous and straightforward in my speech, and I have offended many gentlemen who advocate the mass language, which I deeply regret. However, for some writers who are unreasonably troublemaking, or mocking and abusive, I can only deal with them with an "unceremonious" attitude.

In fact, my words seem to be "anti-mass," but my propositions are all based on the true position of the mass language, and the writers who advocate the mass language are speaking from the objective environment. From the ordinary perspective, there is naturally a big gap between them. Although the propositions are different, the major premise is that they are all seeking the interests of the masses and seeking happiness for the masses, which I think there is not much difference. Or perhaps the "anti-mass" - this newspaper is not anti-mass, because people say we are anti-mass - the propositions are still more practical and more concrete.

Naturally, a newspaper should accommodate opinions from all sides and discuss the core of the problem thoroughly to find a solution, the supplement of this newspaper originally held this attitude, but this newspaper publishes more "anti-mass" - texts, and publishes fewer texts advocating the mass language, because among the submissions, abusive, boring, and texts talking about things outside the problem account for the majority. To save a lot of trouble, we have put these texts aside, which is not any prejudice. This is the absolute attitude of this newspaper in advocating open discussion. If there are any insightful opinions, we are very willing to accept them.

Yesterday, I read Mr. Xu's article "Please Look at the Objective Environment" again, which is clearly directed at the article "To a Heartfelt Friend," but that article still does not talk about the core of the problem, and is still a series of empty and impractical arguments. I could have not replied, but to express my personal proposition and announce the attitude of this newspaper, I have to explain it again.

Mr. Xu's topic is "Please Look at the Objective Environment," and the first sentence I have to declare is that we are now deeply in the middle of the environment, so there is no need to look at the environment again, especially the objective environment. Mr. Xu also said:

"The mass language is related to all problems of the masses, it is not simply a language reform movement,

It is a movement within the entire mass life improvement movement,"

I have long understood this intention. Simply put, it is to transform the environment of the masses, but to transform the environment of the masses, it is already very weak to rely solely on the language movement, and the language movement, without going to actual work, only speaks empty and pleasant words, it is still a set of "empty city tactics," how can people not be anxious? (To be continued)

Black Current

— Chen Liang

As long as the foreman, Li Changmazi, went to the street corner to joke with the porridge-selling girl, everyone felt like prisoners released, taking a breath, bending their legs, and even the movement of blood slowed down.

"Grandma, we're really like oxen!" Little Scabby threw the iron bar on the ground, thumped his own broad chest, and was the first to speak, his eyes secretly fixed on the street corner.

"Oxen, hey, oxen even get fed grass."

"I'd rather be an animal. No wife, no children, no home."

"Who says it's not better to be an animal? That foreign chief engineer's hunting dog eats a big silver dollar's worth of beef a day!"

As long as someone starts the conversation, everyone will join in, one sentence after another, endlessly.

The roller compressor rested by the curb, constantly emitting steam, waiting for the special machine to exert its power, to suppress the rising flames of the underground layer until it was flat. Layer upon layer of hot asphalt solution was poured on.

Large chunks of asphalt were thrown into an iron pot, and countless intense flames licked the bottom of the pot, melting it. Black smoke, carrying a foul odor, filled the air above the road. Those standing by the asphalt pot, pouring the asphalt solution, dragging the hot rolling drum, and the driver of the roller compressor, all had dark, glossy faces.

"Ready to pour!"

Then a large bucket of hot black solution was poured out, shimmering silver in the sun. Several laborers used brooms to spread the solution, extending it to the unpaved areas. A black current!

The people living in the black current were forever subjected to the heat of the fire and the roar of the roller compressor.

The one dragging the roller walked on the molten current covered with only a layer of yellow sand, exerting all his strength to flatten the road surface. The hot air rose from his feet straight to his chest, throat, and head, causing a dizzy spell. Then he heard Li Changmazi's venomous scolding: "Hey! Grandma, at this rate, you might as well 'go to heaven' sooner!"

The large buckle was pressed on his shoulder by the thick hemp rope, feeling like a thousand pounds of weight. The tendons in his neck bulged, and blood vessels were stretched taut all around. His feet felt like they were on a hot iron, burning to his heart. "Grandma, if only I had a pair of ox-hoof-like feet, a horse-neck-like neck. I can't take it."

"Who can take it? We're all living on a volcano, for a few cents." Zhang Banlai took a long breath. His body wasn't strong, and he leaned lazily in the crowd, moaning, "Oh yo lai oh yo, oh yo…"

Everyone moaned:

"Oh yo lai oh yo, oh yo…"

When the roller compressor started moving, the second bucket of asphalt was melting in the iron pot.

The roller compressor, with its bulging belly, struggled to climb past. The second bucket of asphalt solution was poured down. While those working on the edge of the black current could barely breathe, Li Changmazi at the street corner was joking with the porridge-selling girl, also breathless with laughter.

"He's also human! He has the leisure to tease girls." Someone said in the misty smoke.

"Shameless, relying entirely on the foreign devils, sucking up to them, and lording it over us!" The old Shandong man pushing the roller had a quick tongue and always worried others.

"Old fellow, watch your words!" Little Scabby threw coal into the stove while gesturing to him with his mouth.

Page 21

"Grandma, whoever is a traitor, we'll beat him!" The old Shandong man was unconvinced, but, but...

Unexpectedly, a block of asphalt surged over his back, and his feet felt like they were stabbed with dozens of knives, causing him to fall with a piercing scream of "Ah!" His whole body lay on the hot asphalt solution! Everyone used sticks to drag him to a place without asphalt. Everyone's hearts were burning, almost scorched.

The old Shandong man died at that moment, his body black, scorched, and rotten like roasted pork. The troublemaker had long escaped. The foreman, Li Changmazi, scolded all the living, pushing aside the onlookers to make a phone call to the authorities and the Public Works Department. "Damn it, you bunch of bastards, go die! You've gotten me into trouble."

But the third bucket of asphalt was already melting in the iron pot.

Street Urchin

— Hong

Every morning and at five o'clock in the afternoon, a sharp and familiar sound came from the alley:

"Shen Bao - Xin Wen Bao..."

This was the cry of the one the people in the alley called "Little Monkey." He was probably twelve or thirteen years old? He himself wasn't sure. At the same time, he didn't know his own name. His appearance did resemble a monkey, as he was an undernourished and orphaned street urchin! A pair of sunken eyes was embedded in a dark, gaunt face, barely showing a pair of arched eyes. He wore a sleeveless blue cloth shirt and a pair of striped cloth pants, splattered with mud and oil stains, having lost their original color. Whenever the young ladies in the alley met him, they would always cover their noses with small handkerchiefs, or even turn their faces away and spit on the ground.

Was it last winter? The northwest wind howled, and no one lingered in the alley. Children and adults were all inside their houses, telling stories around coal stoves. Only Sister-in-law Er, who went to work at the yarn factory every morning, often saw him wrapped in two burlap sacks, wearing a skullcap without a top, holding an iron hoop in one hand and carrying a broken bamboo basket in the other, standing by the garbage bin picking up scrap paper and rags, looking at people with timid, pale eyes.

One day, Sister-in-law Er felt very sorry for him and gave him a bowl of cold rice. From then on, every time he came to the alley, he would stand and linger at the back door of Sister-in-law Er's house, waiting for Sister-in-law Er to give him a bowl of rice before slowly leaving the alley.

Time passed, and he went from the howling cold wind to this mild spring. His hands and feet turned from red and swollen to dry, firewood-like chips.

It was almost dusk now—

"Xin Ye Bao - Da Mei Evening News..."

The sound was heard again in the alley as usual. In the dim twilight, he stretched his voice and cried out again and again.

However, recently, this sharp and familiar cry has not been heard for quite some time. Whenever there is a silent dusk, I remember Little Monkey. Alas, where has this homeless wanderer drifted to now?

But some people say that the alley has been quiet and easy to sleep in these past few nights, without the strange voice of that Little Monkey!

Sleepless Night

— Simon

After the waning night, the surroundings were a quiet and beautiful world, without a single sound. All sounds had sunk into the black countryside of night. Happy people had long entered sweet dreams, intoxicated in blissful dreams.

But even this blessing I couldn't enjoy.

Like a ghost possessing me, I felt an unprecedented disturbance and agitation. I don't know how many thousands of times I tossed and turned, nothing felt right. Although my eyes were tightly closed, my nerves refused to rest, deliberately obstructing and working. The more I tossed and turned, the more excited I became, and the clearer my thoughts. Memory picked out everything brightly, even some old events that had faded in the past and the sorrows that I feared to arouse all swarmed like ants into my brain.

It was really impossible to sleep anymore. Damn it, I cursed unconsciously. Then I relentlessly pounded on the bed board and grabbed my hair, hoping to exhaust myself as much as possible, so that my body and mind would slowly become drowsy and fall asleep from a gradual daze. But all was in vain. Moving my hands and feet only resulted in a sweat and wasted my energy. The god of sleep still didn't come, and my nerves were still just as clear, not feeling tired at all.

Ought to hate the god of sleep!

I deeply felt that the pain of insomnia was more severe than the pain of heartbreak.

My eyelids were indeed tired to death, and it was very difficult to open them. However, my mind was becoming clearer. What to do? I tried all kinds of methods, but none worked. The clock on the table had struck three times. It was a summer night, and the sun rose especially early. Looking at the sky, it was almost dawn. I tried every way to sleep, but none were effective.

So I didn't sleep anymore. Anyway, I couldn't sleep no matter what. I simply slipped out of bed, turned on the light, lit a cigarette, and paced to the window.

I stood there blankly, rubbing my sleepy eyes. Looking at the sky, the moon had already set. Only a few stars remained, dotting the blue sky listlessly. Suddenly, a cold wind blew over me, causing me to shiver several times, and goosebumps rose on my skin. At the same time, this wind brought a desolate feeling like the lonely night scene, and a desolate tremor immediately surged in my heart. I felt as if I had been abandoned by everything, a similar sadness.

To encounter the same experiences as the unfortunate in the world, these days I have left my family and wandered far away in a foreign land, gritting my teeth to live a poor life. These long days are drowning in the melancholy of lost laughter. The thick dust of life and the heavy clouds of sorrow, lamenting human affairs and personal circumstances, cover my thoughts and my soul like a fog. Because of excessive worry, I have insomnia. And the weight of worry can never be reduced, so the insomnia becomes heavier day by day as the worry increases. Even if worry doesn't break my body, this insomnia is enough to overwhelm a weak life. I haven't had any kind of palpitations because of this, anyway, living is not interesting, and this world will not give me any complete gift. Let the demons of life ravage me at will.

Zheng Xiaoxu and his ilk's so-called "Manchurian Paradise"

Garret Writer

— Jun

Like a pigeon coop, the width of the room wasn't even five feet wide. Putting in two beds and two writing desks, all the space was almost completely occupied. If there were three or five visitors, there was simply no room to stand. It was easy to get through the freezing winter, but once the sweltering summer arrived, life became unbearable. The one window, already as small as it could be, faced west. From the afternoon onwards, the intense sun shone into the room, like a furnace, constantly evaporating waves of suffocating heat. Hiding inside was like being a wonton in a steamer. Large beads of sweat flowed non-stop.

Two fellows lived in this kind of place.

—Where do you live now?—

Whenever someone asked, they all seemed to agree not to answer. If you asked again, "Still in a garret?"

—Of course. If it's not a garret, is it a Western-style house?

The reply had some indignation and sadness in its tone. But this was their usual attitude. A nonchalant smile still floated on their faces.

Living a miserable life forever cramped in a garret, sometimes when they thought about it, they couldn't help but feel sad. But this sadness was usually very brief, and they forgot about it again in no time. In fact, each of them had a not-insignificant income, and it certainly wasn't impossible to rent a more comfortable house. But it was always like this: as soon as they got their money, they spent their days gallivanting around, drinking, dancing, and going to cafes, indulging themselves to the fullest. In just a few days, they would lightly spend all the fruits of their month's hard work.

On the last night before the money ran out, the sky was about to dawn. They dragged their listless feet out of the dance hall. Stumbling along the sidewalk in the middle of the night, like ghosts.

The night wind blew coldly, seemingly clearing up their dazed nerves a bit. One of them said:

—It's really impossible to go on messing around like this. A gallivanting life can only produce some worthless gallivanting things. Upright articles can't be written. In a few days, I'm afraid I won't even be able to write this. It's really like ruining myself. I think I need to be serious from now on, bury myself in creation, and write one or two amazing works.

The other one, after hearing this, only glanced at the one who spoke, without saying a word. He also felt the same way in his heart. But he had lost confidence in himself. After a while, he slowly and softly sighed:

—To be able to produce satisfactory works, you must first make life serious. Like this, it's always just a pipe dream.

Chatting a lot doesn't necessarily mean you can do it. From that moment on, the two of them swore not to go out again, closed the door, and buried themselves in writing. But this was also because the money had run out; otherwise, they would still be as dissolute as before. Every day, from morning till night, they sat at their desks, hating the blank sheets of paper. One was preparing to write a novella, and the other was preparing to write a script of tens of thousands of words. But after half a day, they still couldn't write a single line. They racked their brains but couldn't figure out how to start or come up with a satisfactory story. Sheet after sheet of paper was torn up. In the end, they all threw down their pens and helplessly smoked a cigarette.

"What to do? I want to write, but I can't. What to do?"

A gallivanting life can only produce gallivanting things. My brain is twisted."

Page 22

Page 23

They looked at each other and both sighed deeply for a while.

This sigh actually lasted for several days. And after that, they simply didn't care about anything anymore. They continued to live that kind of disorganized life, becoming more and more decadent. And they desperately wrote some boring manuscripts that couldn't be any more boring. They didn't want to imagine whether the future was bright or dark. They only sought to get through one day at a time. Now, whenever they meet people, they say, "There's no way out for garret writers; we can only continue to decline."

Fiction

Uncle's Braid (4)

— Ling He

The Mid-Autumn Festival that Shi Min had been eagerly awaiting finally passed. Now that he thought about it, everything was quite ordinary except for eating sesame mooncakes that night and the lotus root made into a dragon with red paper. Speaking of that lotus root, Aunt was really extremely clever. She cut the red paper into dragon whiskers and a tail, and then took a few incense sticks from the incense burner, with triangular red flags attached, writing "Peace Under Heaven" and "Abundant Harvest," etc., and inserted them on the dragon's back, how interesting. No one ate the lotus root on Mid-Autumn Night, but it was used to worship the moon all night, until the next morning when Shi Min secretly ate it.

Shi Min did not study this day, from morning to dusk, because his father had been invited to be a "gongqing" (note) for someone, and would usually return very late. He was alone in the garden catching a large grasshopper, and although the grasshopper spat a lot of yellow water on his hands, he was very happy. He came in from the back side door, walked to the back hall, and secretly put the grasshopper on the neck of his aunt, who was embroidering, scaring her to jump up with a loud cry. Then Shi Min laughed and ran away victoriously. He played alone in the garden for a long time, and when he returned to the house, his father had already returned.

Strangely, there were many people gathered in the house, all from the village. Some of them Shi Min recognized, even Uncle Chongyang who had helped harvest rice at home last time was there. There were also some faces that were very familiar, but he couldn't name them. Everyone seemed very excited, not knowing why, as if something had gone wrong. In the middle of them, Shi Min's father was reading the newspaper: Even his mother was listening with rapt attention. Shi Min also squeezed in and out from under other people's arms, wanting to see the pictures he liked in the newspaper. Someone pulled his little braid, how annoying, he turned his head and saw an unfamiliar face smiling at him, he widened his eyes and pursed his lips, expressing his anger, but that person laughed even harder, there was really nothing he could do. The only way was to ignore him and still look over his father's shoulder, watching his father read every word on the newspaper. At this time, he heard Uncle Chongyang talking about the Wuchang Uprising and the restoration of China:

"With this, what else do those Manchus have? You see, it must be the world of the revolutionaries."

"That's not necessarily true. You know the revolutionaries, they have few men and horses."

Shi Min didn't recognize who was speaking. But after a while, no one spoke anymore, and everyone quietly listened to his father reading the newspaper, saying:

"It was rumored before the Mid-Autumn Festival that the revolutionaries had launched an uprising in E'yuan. Initially scheduled for the sixteenth, it could not be completed due to strict prevention. It was then changed to the eighteenth, but it was discovered by a secret agent, and more than 20 revolutionaries were captured, and dozens of boxes of explosives were seized. On the nineteenth, they hastily launched an uprising with the new army, and the city was lost due to the small number of soldiers."

Xu Zhai said, pinching his fingers to count:

"Nineteenth, twentieth, twenty-first, twenty-second... what's today's date?"

"Today is the twenty-sixth." This was the voice of Grey Hen, not knowing when she had come.
